# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

- `sg-evals/servo--be6a2f99` (servo/servo)

{"content":"1: //! The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n5: //! place).\n6: //!\n7: //! ### External view\n8: //!\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\n11: //!\n12: //! 1. Each time the\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n21: //! time). ... (truncated)

Perfect! I've successfully traced the Rust trait solver obligation chain and created a comprehensive answer document. Here's what I discovered:

## Key Files and Components:

**1. ObligationForest (Data Structure)**
- `compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs` - The tree-based data structure managing pending trait obligations

**2. Trait Selection Pipeline**
- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs` - SelectionContext containing the main selection logic
- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs` - Assembles candidate impls that could satisfy obligations
- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs` - Confirms selected candidates by type unification
- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs` - Impl matching logic

**3. Fulfillment Engine**
- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs` - FulfillmentContext manages obligation resolution through the ObligationForest

**4. Error Reporting**
- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs` - Generates diagnostics for unsatisfied trait bounds

## The Obligation Chain:

1. **Entry**: `SelectionContext::select()` → `poly_select()` 
2. **Stack**: Creates TraitObligationStack to track nested obligations and cycles
3. **Assembly**: `assemble_candidates()` collects all applicable impls and bounds
4. **Matching**: `match_impl()` verifies type parameter unification
5. **Evaluation**: Filters and ranks candidates by specificity
6. **Confirmation**: `confirm_candidate()` generates nested obligations
7. **Processing**: `ObligationForest::process_obligations()` recursively processes the obligation tree
8. **Resolution**: Returns success or error for each obligation
9. **Reporting**: `report_fulfill
... (truncated)

 format!(\n78:                     \"downstream crates may implement trait `{trait_desc}`{self_desc}\",\n79:                     trait_desc = trait_ref.print_trait_sugared(),\n80: /// stack. These\n139:     /// participants will then forego caching their results. This is\n140:     /// not the most efficient solution, but it addresses #60010. The\n141:     /// problem we are trying to prevent:\n142:     ///\n143:     /// - If you have `A: AutoTrait` requires `B: AutoTrait` and `C: NonAutoTrait`\n144:     /// - `B: AutoTrait` requires `A: AutoTrait` (coinductive cycle, ok)\n145:     /// - `C: NonAutoTrait` requires `A: AutoTrait` (non-coinductive cycle, not ok)\n146:     ///\n147:     /// you don't want to cache that `B: AutoTrait` or `A: AutoTrait`\n148:     /// is `EvaluatedToOk`; this is because they were only considered\n149:     /// ok on the premise that if `A: AutoTrait` held, but we indeed\n150:     /// encountered a problem (later on) with `A: AutoTrait`.   "content": "{\"content\":\"1: //! The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \\\"backtrace\\\" of each\\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\\n5: //! place).\\n6: //!\\n7: //! ### External view\\n8: //!\\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\\n11: //!\\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\\n14: //!\\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\\n24: //!\\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \\\"true\\\"\\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\\n39: //!   \\\"backtrace\\\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\\n43: //!\\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\\n46: //!\\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\\n49: //!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\\n50: //!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\\n51: //!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\\n52: //!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\\n53: //!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\\n54: //! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\\n55: //!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\\n56: //!\\n57: //! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\\n58: //! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`).     "content": "1: //! The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n5: //! place).\n6: //!\n7: //! ### External view\n8: //!\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\n11: //!\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n14: //!\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n24: //!\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n39: //!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\n43: //!\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\n46: //!\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n49: //!   have also been completed). We don't winnow if there is exactly one\n422:         // candidate. This is a relatively minor distinction but it\n423:         // can lead to better inference and error-reporting. An\n424:         // example would be if there was an impl:\n425:         //\n426:         //     impl<T:Clone> Vec<T> { fn push_clone(...) { ... } }\n427:         //\n428:         // and we were to see some code `foo.push_clone()` where `boo`\n429:         // is a `Vec<Bar>` and `Bar` does not implement `Clone`. If\n430:         // we were to winnow, we'd wind up with zero candidates.\n431:         // Instead, we select the right impl now but report \"`Bar` does\n432:         // not implement `Clone`\".\n433:         if candidates.len() == 1 {\n434:             return self.filter_reservation_impls(candidates.pop().unwrap());\n435:         }\n436: \n437:         // Winnow, but record the exact outcome of evaluation, which\n438:         // is needed for specialization. Propagate overflow if it occurs.\n439:         let candidates = candidates\n440:             .into_iter()\n441:             .map(|c| match self.evaluate_candidate(stack, &c) {\n442:                 Ok(eval) if eval.may_apply() => {\n443:                     Ok(Some(EvaluatedCandidate { candidate: c, evaluation: eval }))\n444:                 }\n445:                 Ok(_) => Ok(None),\n446:                 Err(OverflowError::Canonical) => {\n447:                     Err(SelectionError::Overflow(OverflowError::Canonical))\n448:                 }\n449:                 Err(OverflowError::Error(e)) => {\n450:                     Err(SelectionError::Overflow(OverflowError::Error(e)))\n451: ",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs%3FL300-450"
